  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dede69aa-be6d-4a80-aa8c-8c21b82fc80d'
      });

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/579750087" />
    <a title="Sean Showalter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6092961-sean-showalter"><img alt="Sean Showalter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1382820806p2/6092961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/579750087?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Showalter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Showalter" href="/user/show/6092961-sean-showalter">Sean Showalter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780800754457" href="/book/show/872187.Personality_Plus">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sean by: </span>
      Kenny Cleveland
  </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer579750087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7621982919591853733">This book helped me gain a deep and accurate picture of myself. In addition, it has helped me to understand others. I regret that I was introduced to it so late in my life. In my opinion, this book should be a requisite in every high school in America. I strongly encourage everyone to read it.<br/><br/>Synopsis<br/>There are 4 basic personality types created by some ancient Greek dude back in the day. All of us humans will have characteristics of each type. You take a personality assessment in the beginning of</span>
  <span id="freeText7621982919591853733" style="display:none">This book helped me gain a deep and accurate picture of myself. In addition, it has helped me to understand others. I regret that I was introduced to it so late in my life. In my opinion, this book should be a requisite in every high school in America. I strongly encourage everyone to read it.<br /><br />Synopsis<br />There are 4 basic personality types created by some ancient Greek dude back in the day. All of us humans will have characteristics of each type. You take a personality assessment in the beginning of the book to determine your strongest types. If you're like me, you'll have 1 dominant type, and a second sub-dominant type. It seems that most of us are wired that way, but that is not always the case. Some of us will be more balanced.<br /><br />Then the book goes into detail about the strengths/weaknesses of each type and how to overcome your handicaps and accept them in others. The author further offers some suggestions on how to improve relations with people based on the knowledge of the different personality types and being able to identify those in yourself and others.<br /><br />I had many "holy cow!" moments when reading this book and found it a real joy. Anytime I learn amazing and insightful information that is instantly applicable to my life I get excited! This book will change your life if you've never been exposed to this information before.<br /><br />My perspective has changed as a result of the information passed on to me from reading Personality Plus and the author has delivered on her intent on making a "better me" through the understanding of different personality types and the application of that new-found knowledge in my personal relationships.<br /><br />Need I say more? :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="7621982919591853733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_71764073" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71764073" />
    <a title="Kate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1990201-kate"><img alt="Kate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405115471p2/1990201.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71764073?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate" href="/user/show/1990201-kate">Kate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71764073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8909373240050573801">I thought this book was pretty gimmicky. The conceit of it is that there are four basic "temperaments": Popular Sanguine, Peaceful Phlegmatic, Powerful Choleric, and Perfect Melancholy. The idea is that you can identify your own tendencies and those of the people you interact with, and adapt suitably. For example, Popular Sanguines are fun, talkative, outgoing, have great ideas & get fired up about them, but they are flaky, self-centered, & lack organization & follow through. So maybe they could</span>
  <span id="freeText8909373240050573801" style="display:none">I thought this book was pretty gimmicky. The conceit of it is that there are four basic "temperaments": Popular Sanguine, Peaceful Phlegmatic, Powerful Choleric, and Perfect Melancholy. The idea is that you can identify your own tendencies and those of the people you interact with, and adapt suitably. For example, Popular Sanguines are fun, talkative, outgoing, have great ideas &amp; get fired up about them, but they are flaky, self-centered, &amp; lack organization &amp; follow through. So maybe they could lead the meeting and get everyone excited, but then delegate so that others will get the details properly taken care of. Perfect Melancholies are introverted and analytical, organized, easily depressed, and pessimistic. Powerful Cholerics are extroverted optimistic "doers" who make good leaders, but can be controlling, bossy, and stubborn, &amp; don't have much use for friends. Peaceful Phlegmatics are easy-going, happy, relaxed, but unexciting, resistant to change, &amp; can seem wishy-washy or lazy because they are laid-back.<br />My first "problem" with this book is the test one can take to identify their type. There were forty rows of words, four across, and you must select which one of each row of four best applies to you. The thing that I found weird was that each set of four words had nothing necessarily in common other than starting with the same letter, which to me seems like an odd contrivance. For example, instead of deciding where you are on a continuum, like "shy, reserved, outgoing, or bold" you must decide if you are:<br />persistent, playful, persuasive, or peaceful<br />refreshing, reserved, respectful, or resourceful<br />orderly, obliging, outspoken, or optimistic<br />impatient, insecure, indecisive, or interrupts<br />worrier, withdrawn, workaholic, or wants credit<br /><br />I think that you can get a murky idea at best, as several or none of the words from each row might fit you. Then on top of that, you can end up with a fairly even distribution between two or more types, so you are, say, a sanguine with choleric tendencies, or whatever.<br />So basically, it comes down to: There are all different types of people out there who think and behave differently, have different strengths &amp; weaknesses, get along well or not well with certain other personalities or situations, and respond well to different types of communication &amp; behavior. Gee, thanks! I never knew that different people are, um, different from one another.<br />The take-away from this book, I guess, is to pay attention to yourself &amp; others, and try to play to your own &amp; one another's strengths, and try to mitigate weaknesses. Which is good advice, of course. But although there are some good (if seemingly overstated) examples, it is not rocket science, or really, any kind of science.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8909373240050573801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1011180747" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1011180747" />
    <a title="Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6665735-books"><img alt="Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419956881p2/6665735.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1011180747?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Books" href="/user/show/6665735-books">Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780800754457" href="/book/show/872187.Personality_Plus">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6665735-books?shelf=reviewed-2014">reviewed-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1011180747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18077042572307930948">I very seldom read non-fiction, and even less than that do I read self-help books. That’s more hubby’s kind of thing. Me? I love my fiction. A few months ago at the office, a colleague was telling me about a book he and his wife were reading that teaches you to understand who you are and thus will help you understand others. The way he explained it, I was intrigued, and naturally I also wanted to read this book which sounded as though it might have life-changing powers. I have an analytical mind</span>
  <span id="freeText18077042572307930948" style="display:none">I very seldom read non-fiction, and even less than that do I read self-help books. That’s more hubby’s kind of thing. Me? I love my fiction. A few months ago at the office, a colleague was telling me about a book he and his wife were reading that teaches you to understand who you are and thus will help you understand others. The way he explained it, I was intrigued, and naturally I also wanted to read this book which sounded as though it might have life-changing powers. I have an analytical mind, and it just so happens that this book agrees that I have, so it should come as no surprise then that the minute said colleague borrowed me his copy of Personality Plus, I jumped right in. I even discovered what sort of personality hubby has (Peaceful Phlegmatic) and how it balances out with my own personality (Perfect Melancholy). <br /><br />The book is infused with humor and the descriptions of each personality (there are four) are short and to the point. No unnecessarily long and tedious descriptions, and the author uses scenarios of her and her husband’s experiences (before and after they knew about the different personality types) which often had me smiling and to which I could easily relate.<br /><br />Did this book change my life? Only time will tell. It was informative and interesting, and made me realize that there are things about us we simply cannot change. We can, however, adapt and compromise, but most personality traits, the ones we are born with, are nearly impossible to change. For instance: my personality type (Perfect Melancholy) cannot deal with chaos and disorder. I’m idealistic, I like lists, I like to analyze problems and study people, and I want things in my life to be in a neat and orderly fashion. My motto: if it’s worth doing, it’s worth doing right. I’ll never compromise on quality. Those are the things about myself I cannot change. I can change my bad habits, my negative thought patterns, and improve myself in little ways, but I cannot change the traits with which I was born. I always knew this, but now I have a firm understanding of what the difference is between personality and habits formed over the course of my life without realizing it has become habit. Maybe now I won’t be so hard on myself.<br /><br />Another important insight I gained from this book is how my personality stacks up with hubby’s. His personality (Peaceful Phlegmatic) includes being easygoing and relaxed (which, to my dismay, might explain why we’re always late for appointments). According to Personality Plus he is also agreeable, good under pressure, easy to get along with, and doesn’t get upset easily. It sounds like we’re a good match, and I agree. Like any other marriage, we also have our quarrels and disagreements, but at least now I understand him a little bit better. <br /><br />So there you have it. It’s probably not a life-changing read, but it might make a difference in your way of thinking if you take the time to understand the four different personality types. It also helped me to understand certain things about my children, and how to deal with their behavior. Final verdict: Personality Plus is without a doubt a worthwhile read. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18077042572307930948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15954238545917051791">I do not exaggerate when I tell you this book saved my family. We had 4 children we homeschooled until high school. I was a full time homemaker and on call 24/7. I was stressed out, worn out, and guilted out by my inability to communicate effectively with these 4 short humans. I thought I would lose my mind! Then, probably about 1987, I read this book and it changed my life and the lives of my kids (and husband). It has held me in good stead through church activities, jobs, public school meeting</span>
  <span id="freeText15954238545917051791" style="display:none">I do not exaggerate when I tell you this book saved my family. We had 4 children we homeschooled until high school. I was a full time homemaker and on call 24/7. I was stressed out, worn out, and guilted out by my inability to communicate effectively with these 4 short humans. I thought I would lose my mind! Then, probably about 1987, I read this book and it changed my life and the lives of my kids (and husband). It has held me in good stead through church activities, jobs, public school meetings and a dozen other situations.<br /><br />This book will give you the tools to roughly categorize the temperaments of the people in your life and reveal to you how to love them, live with them, and work with them. What job will most likely satisfy a co-worker or committee member. Why certain people just aren't "cut out" for certain jobs. And why your husband insists on every book on the shelf being the same height irregardless of any other issues.<br /><br />It's simple and straightforward, easy to read and understand, and most important? It's easy to implement. Every HR director should have to read this book. It's a gem.</span>

<div id="review_2786682374" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2786682374" />
    <a title="Charissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3848272-charissa"><img alt="Charissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514647430p2/3848272.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2786682374?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2019</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3848272-charissa?shelf=favorite-reads">favorite-reads</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2786682374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17327306069693276379">This book blew me away. I didn't pick it up with any serious intention of really enjoying it. I thought it'd be another boring book to help explain personalities and help me as I write characters for my books. But this was a pleasant, inspiring surprise. As I did the personality test and began delving deeper into the book, I stopped only reading for intellectual/working knowledge and started learning about myself. The title said I would, but I hadn't believe it. :) Now I do.<br/><br/>This really helped me</span>
  <span id="freeText17327306069693276379" style="display:none">This book blew me away. I didn't pick it up with any serious intention of really enjoying it. I thought it'd be another boring book to help explain personalities and help me as I write characters for my books. But this was a pleasant, inspiring surprise. As I did the personality test and began delving deeper into the book, I stopped only reading for intellectual/working knowledge and started learning about myself. The title said I would, but I hadn't believe it. :) Now I do.<br /><br />This really helped me discover things about myself I had never pieced together in my 50 years of life. As I began to understand why I did things certain ways or was bothered by certain traits in others, and then learned about other temperaments and why they did things the way they did--I could see family members, friends, associates in all the different personalities...and it explained so much about why they are like they are or do what they do. <br /><br />I highly recommend this book to everyone. I feel that it made me understand not only myself better, but others as well...and I feel more confident that when I go into a room with a large amount of people next time, I will be a lot less judgmental, a lot more patient, and a lot more understanding with how everyone acts differently in the same situation. And I will appreciate that we all are so different and thank God for the differences even. <br /><br />One of my favorite things about this book was how it encourages the reader to play to your strengths and overcome the weaknesses inherent in each personality so you can become the best You possible. It really was inspirational. I took tons of notes and plan on studying them and working on my weaknesses and strengthening my strengths in the future. I read this on Kindle Unlimited, but like it enough that I plan on buying my own copy for future reference. It's one I want to have sitting on my library shelf. </span>

  <span id="freeText4663167951107307117" style="display:none">I am giving it 4/5 because it had too much repetitive content and the author could have made it shorter.<br /><br />The book taught me a lot of things it's very useful for the starters who want to understand themselves and others, also how to get along with others and accept themselves the way they are.<br /><br />Florence in Personality Plus teaches us about four temperaments. Each person may have one temperament dominant, he may also have two matching temperaments or two opposites, or he may have all four of them at the same time but with different levels, but most importantly she teaches us how each type makes the person think in a particular way, it's really important to understand your type so you can accept who you are the way you are.<br />The book really took some pressure off my shoulders because being of perfect melancholy type I always thought of everything and examined everything carefully and always thought why am I like this, I wanted to change myself, change my way of thinking but now I feel comfortable the way I am because that's my type. Another thing that I hated about myself was that I'm not much of an outgoing person and I lose most of my energy if I spend my day with others but now I can understand also that's because of my melancholy/phlegmatic personality and I'm accepting it as it's.<br /><br />Overall I think the book is good except it has too much repetitive content.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564209-siobhain?shelf=family-favorites">family-favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer4458027606710198012">Personality Plus was helpful for our family when we read it almost twenty years ago. Like most families, we had the most trouble between family members with widely different temperaments because both children and adults could only see the world through their own ways of thinking and reacting. Personality Plus helped each member of our family to understand and appreciate his own temperament as well as the temperaments of each other. In a lighthearted manner, Mrs. Littauer illustrates the differen</span>
  <span id="freeText4458027606710198012" style="display:none">Personality Plus was helpful for our family when we read it almost twenty years ago. Like most families, we had the most trouble between family members with widely different temperaments because both children and adults could only see the world through their own ways of thinking and reacting. Personality Plus helped each member of our family to understand and appreciate his own temperament as well as the temperaments of each other. In a lighthearted manner, Mrs. Littauer illustrates the different temperaments with infectiously humorous stories. Most of our family reading sessions included many laughs as we read the book aloud together. The children would later enjoy rereading the funny stories to themselves. Are you a Popular Sanguine, a Perfect Melancholy, a Powerful Choleric, or a Peaceful Phlegmatic? Today there are helpful tests online to help you make this determination, but reading this book helps one to see each temperament in relationship to others and will help anyone to appreciate the different temperaments. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4458027606710198012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1795494050" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1795494050" />
    <a title="Andrea Norton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7258661-andrea-norton"><img alt="Andrea Norton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571800131p2/7258661.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1795494050?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea Norton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea Norton" href="/user/show/7258661-andrea-norton">Andrea Norton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7258661-andrea-norton?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7258661-andrea-norton?shelf=reference">reference</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7258661-andrea-norton?shelf=2016-all-books">2016-all-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7258661-andrea-norton?shelf=2016-growth">2016-growth</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7258661-andrea-norton?shelf=self-help">self-help</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7258661-andrea-norton?shelf=relationships">relationships</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1795494050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7346951911826550693">While I have it set at two stars, it's actually a 1.5 star book, in my opinion. <br/><br/>I picked up Personality Plus at the store because it sounded fun and interesting. Self help books have become a huge part of my life since Christmas 2015, when I had a serious mental crash and put myself through a rigorous "get better" program. Included in the broad category of self help are personality books. I read them for fun now, but also to learn, grow and see things from different perspective. <br/><br/>First, I have to</span>
  <span id="freeText7346951911826550693" style="display:none">While I have it set at two stars, it's actually a 1.5 star book, in my opinion. <br /><br />I picked up Personality Plus at the store because it sounded fun and interesting. Self help books have become a huge part of my life since Christmas 2015, when I had a serious mental crash and put myself through a rigorous "get better" program. Included in the broad category of self help are personality books. I read them for fun now, but also to learn, grow and see things from different perspective. <br /><br />First, I have to get this out of the way: I have never met any man who has ever even dreamed of talking to his wife the way Littauer's husband talks to her. She is "embarrassing," "stupid," and "wrong," so often that I began to despise reading about him. This isn't a clash of personalities - this is a person who has a problem. Trying to change her core, who she is... that's not okay and not something to model yourself after. <br /><br />Some of the stories in this book are flat out unbelievable. I had a hard time taking anything away from them because they're so out there, so first-world problems that nothing could be gained from them. I understand the world is full of many types of people, but nearly all of them are uptight, cushioned individuals? No. Not even close. <br /><br />While this is a quick read, there is not much depth here at all. Maybe it's because I'm coming off of some really serious, mind-blowing books. Maybe it's because I was so distracted and put off by most of the people used as examples. Maybe I just expected too much from this one. Whatever it is, this book fell extremely flat for me. <br /><br />I enjoy books with tests and exercises in them. They're fun, interesting and can teach you a lot about yourself. However, the personality test in this one seemed more of words put together without any relation to each other. I found it difficult to choose between some of the choices because they didn't relate at all.<br /><br />I can't recommend this one, unfortunately. If you do pick it up, read it with an open mind but a healthy dose of skepticism. This book has been very useful and life changing to other readers, but it just didn't do it for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7346951911826550693" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2733009088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer489021727859838497">I loved this book. It was very helpful in understanding my own temperament and those around me.<br/><br/>I felt some of it was a little klunky as a read, but all in all, a great read with a lot of good information.<br/><br/>But maybe that's just my melancholic nature speaking. Lol.<br/><br/>I would definitely recommend this book to others. I think it could help a lot of people and increase tolerance and understanding.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3064106715" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3064106715" />
    <a title="Jenna Whalen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53480519-jenna-whalen"><img alt="Jenna Whalen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457380958p2/53480519.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3064106715?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenna Whalen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenna Whalen" href="/user/show/53480519-jenna-whalen">Jenna Whalen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780800754457" href="/book/show/872187.Personality_Plus">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3064106715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17916793541014956680">I am a huge fan of personality tests (especially the enneagram), so I was curious about this book and this specific personality test.<br/><br/>I have to say I don't think Personality Plus is a good personality test or way to grow. Any personality thing where there are 4 options immediately raises a red flag for me. You're telling me every person fits into 1 of 4 categories? Yes, I understand everyone has a unique blend of categories with one being higher than most (usually), but only 4 is way too little. </span>
  <span id="freeText17916793541014956680" style="display:none">I am a huge fan of personality tests (especially the enneagram), so I was curious about this book and this specific personality test.<br /><br />I have to say I don't think Personality Plus is a good personality test or way to grow. Any personality thing where there are 4 options immediately raises a red flag for me. You're telling me every person fits into 1 of 4 categories? Yes, I understand everyone has a unique blend of categories with one being higher than most (usually), but only 4 is way too little. Look at the enneagram and MBI. They have over double.<br /><br />As I was reading this, I thought each type sounded like an extremely unhealthy version of certain enneagram numbers. And each story about someone she gave made me think, "this person sounds extremely unhealthy and terrible. Why does anyone want to hang out with them?" I also thought that she had to be exaggerating because there is no way people actually act like the stories she told (she did say her type does tend to exaggerate stories, so in the back of my mind I kept wondering if she was falling into this).<br /><br />Bottom line, I would not recommend this personality test to help you see your strengths and weaknesses (also let's talk about how this book classifies introversion as a weakness *rolls eyes*). This is a very limiting test and won't help you get out of your box. I didn't see myself as any of this types - a little bit of a few of them, sure, but I can't say I'm definitely one type over the other. If you want to grow and work on weaknesses, please look into a different personality test (I highly suggest the enneagram).</span>
  <a data-text-id="17916793541014956680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/614442750" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/614442750?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greg Frucci" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greg Frucci" href="/user/show/9849177-greg-frucci">Greg Frucci</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780800754457" href="/book/show/872187.Personality_Plus">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9849177-greg-frucci?shelf=wisdom">wisdom</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer614442750" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer592905278513971228">I have found a love for understanding personalities including my own. This is the third book I have read on the subject lately, and this one is the best so far. Florence Littauer has created a fun book to read with a core message of understanding why we think and act the way we do. The most important chapter is Chapter 16 where she made me realize that she is not placing me in a "box", but allowing me to exit my Way in order to understand and accept how others are who seem so much different than</span>
  <span id="freeText592905278513971228" style="display:none">I have found a love for understanding personalities including my own. This is the third book I have read on the subject lately, and this one is the best so far. Florence Littauer has created a fun book to read with a core message of understanding why we think and act the way we do. The most important chapter is Chapter 16 where she made me realize that she is not placing me in a "box", but allowing me to exit my Way in order to understand and accept how others are who seem so much different than I. We all have aspects of the four major personalities or combinations of the four. We simply have some which are stonger than others. I am not the "whoo hoo" type and I would always wonder why anyone would act and be so loud...but that is just them being them...now I can just smile and say..."oh, right, they are a Sanguine" and accept the difference...even take a bit of how they are and apply it to myself. (I'm a Melancholy/Choleric by the way...the terms will make sense if you read the book).<br /><br />If you have a relationship with someone and aspects of them bug the crap out of you, this book will help. If you want to have some fun while people watching, this book will give you much insight. The greatest benefit after reading the book perhaps will be a smile on your face as you say to yourself, "ah ha...I am neither "right nor wrong"...I just Am...and so is everybody else."</span>
  <a data-text-id="592905278513971228" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103644283" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8691851168959098562">This is a great reference if you want to understand yourself better and understand the others around you as well. It's always good to know your strengths and weaknesses as a friend, a worker, and even as a parent. This book is indeed a plus since it also makes you look into other people's strengths and weaknesses. Knowing, understanding and appreciating other persons' personalities make working together more possible ... more peaceful.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              >

Examples and anecdotes serve a purpose, but the book was wholly narrative. I expected a lot more content, and a little less giddiness. Was not a fan.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0son5J4V04BnJlqhYEzNPe0M5s84I/Wwosw6yyRQXgmcj5ynb4j4JUIVleeXXaKHlx6J/ktClFvhUphww/C+dA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Hace más de 50 años, Les Giblin nos enseñó cómo mediante el sabio manejo de los principios básicos del comportamiento humano es viable asegurar el éxito en el mundo profesional, —y en cualquier faceta de la vida. En la actualidad, como miles de lectores lo afirman, su filosofía es más vigente hoy que nunca antes. En este valioso libro el lector hallará acertadas técnicas para desarrollar confianza en sus relaciones interpersonales, de negocios y sociales, las cuales van desde pequeños trucos de lenguaje corporal que rara vez notamos en nosotros mismos (pero casi siempre en los demás) hasta el acertado manejo de sus mejores habilidades. Cómo tener confianza y seguridad en las relaciones interpersonales le ayuda a obtener lo que usted en realidad necesita y quiere en el trato con quienes le rodean de manera íntegra y sin complicaciones. Las técnicas probadas de Les Giblin le enseñarán cómo:  Descubrir los secretos esenciales que se encuentran en la naturaleza humana para influenciar a los demás. Controlar las actitudes y expectativas de otros a través de su comportamiento.Desarrollar tres de los secretos más efectivos para atraer a la gente.  Considerado uno de los pioneros de la industria del desarrollo personal, Leslie T. Giblin fue premiado como Vendedor Nacional del Año en 1965 y en 1968 escribió su clásico Skill With People. Trascendiendo generaciones, el mensaje siempre vigente de Les Giblin acerca de tener “don de gentes” como una de las habilidades esenciales para la vida adquiere un nuevo significado en esta era de Key project management processes, infrastructure, and the role of the project office.\n\n\n\nControl Through Influence. Productive leadership styles, reciprocity, and maintaining relationships.\n\n\n\nControl Through Project Metrics. Quantitative, predictive, diagnostic, and retrospective metrics for project control, motivating desired behaviors, and avoiding potential problems.\n\n\n\nControl Through Project Initiation. The role of the sponsor in project control, the importance of project vision, project launch documentation, and the project start-up workshop.\n\n\n\nControl Through Project Planning. Collaborative planning as the foundation of project control; planning as a key factor in setting baselines and establishing metrics.\n\n\n\nControl During Project Execution. Measurement and interpretation of project status, informal communication, and maintaining relationships as keys to maintaining control.\n\n\n\nControl Through Tracking and Monitoring. <span id="freeTextContainer10119436616956215938">Florence Littauer is a Christian self-help author and public speaker. Littauer is best known for her series of books based upon the Personality Plus personality system. She was listed as one of Helen K. Hosier's "100 Christian Women Who Changed the Twentieth Century" and has received the National Speakers Association's Council of Peers Award for Excellence and has been designated by them as a Cert</span>
  <span id="freeText10119436616956215938" style="display:none">Florence Littauer is a Christian self-help author and public speaker. Littauer is best known for her series of books based upon the Personality Plus personality system. She was listed as one of Helen K. Hosier's "100 Christian Women Who Changed the Twentieth Century" and has received the National Speakers Association's Council of Peers Award for Excellence and has been designated by them as a Certified Speaking Professional.<br /><br />--From Wikipedia</span>
